## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (ODE growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, so this is a classic single-species population dynamics problem modeled by ordinary differential equations with density dependence and possibly time-varying (environmental) forcing via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth with constant per-capita rate)
- Linear birth–death with immigration: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (constant inflow plus net per-capita growth/decline)
- Density-dependent (quadratic) regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding via negative c1; simplest nonlinearity)
- Verhulst logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) (carrying capacity at P = c1)
- Richards / generalized logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**c2) (variable sharpness of approach to carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric approach to carrying capacity; log-density dependence)
- Theta-logistic (per-capita power density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**(c2 + 1) (flexible density dependence in mortality/competition term)
- Strong Allee effect (bistability): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) * (P / c2 - 1) (additional threshold at P = c2)
- Weak Allee effect (reduced growth at low P): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) * (P / (P + c2)) (low-density limitation without negative growth at very small P)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 (fixed removal rate; possible extinction if c2 too large)
- Proportional harvesting / exploitation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 * P (per-capita removal; shifts effective growth rate)
- Saturating harvest (Holling type removal): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (limited effort/handling causes saturation in removal)
- Time-varying per-capita rate (trend): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (environmental change causing accelerating/declining growth rate)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - P / c4) (periodic environment modulating growth and carrying capacity dynamics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth interpretation: structures of the form dP_dt = P * g(P,t) indicate g(P,t) is the per-capita rate; plotting dP_dt / P vs P often reveals the density-dependence functional form.
- Carrying capacity signature: factors like (1 - P / K) or (1 - (P / K)**nu) imply a stable equilibrium near P = K and a sign change of dP_dt around that value.
- Allee threshold signature: additional factor (P / A - 1) creates another zero of dP_dt at P = A, implying negative growth below A (bistability/extinction threshold).
- Asymmetry in approach to equilibrium: a log term log(K / P) (Gompertz) produces slower growth near K and different curvature than polynomial crowding, often fitting sigmoids with early rapid growth and long tail.
- Harvesting shifts equilibria: subtracting c2 (constant yield) can create multiple equilibria and extinction risk; subtracting c2 * P mainly reduces the effective intrinsic growth rate without introducing a hard threshold by itself.
- Saturating removal signature: subtracting c * P / (P + h) yields near-linear removal at low P but bounded removal at high P, often preventing dP_dt from becoming too negative at large P.
- Time-forcing detection: dependence on t through sin(c*t) suggests periodic/seasonal forcing; through polynomials (c0 + c1*t) suggests secular environmental change.
- Low-density behavior diagnostic: if dP_dt scales like P for small P, growth is approximately exponential at low density; if it scales like P**2 (or higher), strong mate limitation or cooperative effects may be present.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG9)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 77

Let \(A=0.1699888096710614\), \(a=1.0472843670254641\), \(b=10.210545156320043\), \(k=0.09709294493863778\).

GT:
\[
A\Big[(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P + (1-P/b)P + (1-e^{-kP})P\Big].
\]
First two bracketed terms simplify:
\[
(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P + (1-P/b)P = (1-P/b)P\big[(-1+P/a)+1\big]=(1-P/b)P(P/a).
\]
So GT becomes
\[
A\left[\frac{P^2}{a}\left(1-\frac{P}{b}\right) + P\left(1-e^{-kP}\right)\right]
= A\left(\frac{1}{a}P^2 - \frac{1}{ab}P^3 + P - P e^{-kP}\right).
\]
Thus GT is a sum of a cubic polynomial part plus a term \(-A\,P e^{-kP}\). No \(t\)-dependence.

Key structural requirement for any candidate to match (even on a plausible domain like \(P\ge 0\)): it must be able to produce exactly a term of the form \(P e^{-kP}\) (with negative coefficient) and also match the polynomial coefficients. Candidates that only have \(e^{(+c|P|)}\), logs, trig, rationals, etc., cannot equal \(e^{-kP}\) for all \(P\) on any interval unless they degenerate (e.g., coefficient 0), but GT’s exponential term is nonzero.

Now check candidates:

1. Polynomial + \(P c_3 e^{c_4|P|}\) + constant + \(t\)-oscillation. Can kill \(t\)-term by \(c_6=0\). But exponential is \(e^{c_4|P|}\), not \(e^{-kP}\). On \(P\ge0\), it’s \(e^{c_4P}\); to match \(e^{-kP}\) we’d need \(c_4=-k\), giving \(e^{-kP}\) but with **\(+\)** sign: term is \(+P c_3 e^{-kP}\). We could set \(c_3=-A\) to get \(-A P e^{-kP}\). However GT also has polynomial terms \(A(\frac1a P^2-\frac1{ab}P^3+P)\) and candidate has \(P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + P c_2 + c_5\). Set \(c_0=-A/(ab)\), \(c_1=A/a\), \(c_2=A\), \(c_5=0\). This matches exactly on domain \(P\ge0\) (to remove \(|P|\) issue). **Match possible.**

2. Similar but \(t\)-term is \(c_6\exp(c_7\cos(\cdot))\), can set \(c_6=0\). Remaining same as (1): can match on \(P\ge0\) by choosing \(c_4=-k\), \(c_3=-A\), and polynomial coefficients as above, \(c_5=0\). **Match possible.**

3. Rational terms plus \(P^{c_4} c_5 e^{c_6|P|}\). Hard to get exact cubic polynomial unless denominator cancels (would require \(c_1=0\) giving division by \(P\), not polynomial). Also exponential term is \(P^{c_4}e^{c_6|P|}\) not \(P e^{-kP}\) unless \(c_4=1\) and \(c_6=-k\) and domain \(P\ge0\); but still the rational pieces won’t match a pure polynomial globally on an interval. **No.**

4. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), \(P^{c_2}\), constant, and \(\log(c_6 e^{Pc_7}+1)\). Log cannot equal \(-P e^{-kP}\) on an interval. **No.**

5. Like (1) plus \(t\)-sine term; set sine coefficient \(c_6=0\). Then identical matching logic as (1): choose constants and domain \(P\ge0\). **Match possible.**

6. Cubic in \((Pc_3+1)^3\), square roots, \(e^{Pc_8}\). Cannot reproduce polynomial+certain exponential \(P e^{-kP}\) exactly. **No.**

7. Has \(P^3,P^2,P^{1+c_2}\), \(P\log(\cdot)\), linear. No \(P e^{-kP}\). **No.**

8. Has trig(log) and \(\log(c_7 e^{Pc_8}+1)\), no \(P e^{-kP}\). **No.**

9. Logs and \(e^{Pc_7}\log(\cdot)\), not \(P e^{-kP}\). **No.**

13–15. Variants of (1) but with extra cosine/log terms; can set those extra coefficients to 0. Then reduce to polynomial + \(P c_3 e^{c_4|P|}\) + constant. Same as (1): match on \(P\ge0\) with \(c_4=-k\), \(c_3=-A\), polynomial coefficients, constant 0. **Match possible** for 13, 14, 15.

If \(c_2=0\), remaining is \(P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + P c_4 + P c_5 e^{c_6|P|} + c_7\). This can match GT exactly like (1) by setting \(c_6=-k\), \(c_5=-A\), \(c_0=-A/(ab)\), \(c_1=A/a\), \(c_4=A\), \(c_7=0\), domain \(P\ge0\). **Match possible.**

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.17*(−1 + P/1.047)*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − exp(−0.097*P))*P
```

Let me expand this:

**Term 1:** `0.17*(P/1.047 − 1)*(1 − P/10.21)*P`
= `0.17*(P/1.047 − 1)*(1 − P/10.21)*P`

Let me expand `(P/1.047 − 1)*(1 − P/10.21)`:
= `P/1.047 − P²/(1.047×10.21) − 1 + P/10.21`
= `−1 + P(1/1.047 + 1/10.21) − P²/10.69`

So Term 1 = `0.17*P*[−1 + P(0.9551 + 0.0979) − P²×0.09354]`
= `0.17*[−P + 1.053P² − 0.09354P³]`

**Term 2:** `0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P`
= `0.17*[P − P²/10.21]`
= `0.17*P − 0.17*P²/10.21`

**Term 3:** `0.17*(1 − exp(−0.097P))*P`
= `0.17*P − 0.17*P*exp(−0.097P)`

Combining all terms:

**P³ term:** `−0.17×0.09354×P³ ≈ −0.0159P³`
**P² term:** `0.17×1.053P² − 0.17P²/10.21 ≈ 0.179P² − 0.01665P² = 0.1624P²`
**P term:** `−0.17P + 0.17P + 0.17P = 0.17P`
**Exponential term:** `−0.17P×exp(−0.097P)`

So GT ≈ `a*P³ + b*P² + c*P + d*P*exp(−e*P)` where a < 0, b > 0, c > 0, d < 0, e > 0.

The GT has the functional form: **P³ + P² + P + P·exp(−kP)** (with specific coefficients).

This is the key structure: a cubic polynomial in P plus a term `P*exp(negative*P)`.

Note: The GT does NOT depend on `t`.

Now let me check candidates. For P ≥ 0, `|P| = P`, so `exp(c*|P|)` = `exp(c*P)`.

## Checking Candidates

**Candidates with the form P³ + P² + P + P·exp(c·P) + constant:**

Candidates 1, 2, 5, 13, 14, 15, 17, 19, 20, 21, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 28, 57, 58, 59, 61, 62 have `P*exp(c*|P|)` terms.

The GT has form: `c0*P³ + c1*P² + c2*P + c3*P*exp(c4*P)` (no constant term at P=0, GT gives 0).

Let me verify GT(0) = 0. Yes, every term has a factor of P.

**Candidate 25:** `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(c4*|P|) + c5`

Setting c5=0, this gives `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(c4*P)` for P≥0. This matches the GT structure exactly! We need c4 < 0 to match exp(−0.097P).

Candidate 25 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 21:** `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4*exp(c5*|P|) + c6`
= `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*(c2+c3) + P*c4*exp(c5*P) + c6`. Setting c6=0, same structure.

Candidate 21 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 20:** `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P²*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4*exp(c5*|P|) + P*c6 + c7`
= `P³*c0 + P²*(c1+c2) + P*(c3+c6) + P*c4*exp(c5*P) + c7`. Setting c7=0, same structure.

Candidate 20 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 22:** Same idea with redundant terms. Setting c9=0 and combining: matches.

Candidate 22 verdict: [MATCH]

Candidate 23 verdict: [MATCH]

Now let me systematically check ALL candidates. I'll focus on whether each can reduce to `a*P³ + b*P² + c*P + d*P*exp(e*P)`.

**Candidate 1:** Has `exp(c7*t)*cos(c8*t+c9)` — set c6=0 to eliminate t-dependence. Remaining: P³+P²+P+P·exp. Set c5=0.

**Candidate 3:** `P⁴c0/(P+c1) + P³c2/(P+c1) + P²c3/(P+c1) + P^c4·c5·exp(c6·|P|)`. The rational part = `(c0·P⁴+c2·P³+c3·P²)/(P+c1)`. By polynomial division this gives `c0·P³ + (c2−c0·c1)P² + ...` plus a remainder. The last term `P^c4` with free c4: set c4=1 to get `P·c5·exp(c6·P)`. This can match.

**Candidate 12:** `[P⁴c0+P³c2+P³c3·exp(c4|P|)+P²c5·exp(c4|P|)+P²c6]/(P+c1)`. This has exp terms divided by (P+c1). Can this equal P³+P²+P+P·exp? Let me check: multiply GT by (P+c1). We'd need `(a·P³+b·P²+c·P+d·P·exp(eP))·(P+c1) = c0P⁴+c2P³+c3P³exp+c5P²exp+c6P²`. The left side has terms like d·P²·exp and d·c1·P·exp. But the right side has P³·exp and P²·exp but no P·exp term. So we'd need d·c1=0, meaning either d=0 (losing exp) or c1=0 (division by P). If c1=0: `P³c0+P²c2+P²c3·exp+P·c5·exp+P·c6`. This gives P³+P²+P·exp+P but no pure P² without exp and no P·exp separately matching. Actually with c1=0: the expression becomes `P³c0+P²(c2+c6)+P²c3·exp+Pc5·exp`. We need the exp terms to combine to P·exp: c3·P²·exp + c5·P·exp = P·exp·(c3P+c5). This isn't the same as just P·exp(eP) unless c3=0, giving P³c0+P²(c2+c6)+Pc5·exp. Missing the linear P term without exp.
